Part 36 Section 36.14: Wave 64 ARC-AGI-1 Rules

Wave 64 added two new named rules to arc_benchmark.pl targeting two previously unsolved tasks.

Rule A: frame_stamp_at_zero_interior (task 890034e9).

Input: a grid containing exactly one colored rectangular frame. The frame's border cells all share
a single color V that appears nowhere else in the grid; the frame's interior is entirely zero.
The rule identifies the unique source frame, records its interior dimensions IH x IW, then scans
the grid for every IH x IW all-zero rectangular region whose surrounding border cells would fit
within the grid. For each such region the rule stamps a copy of the source frame border (color V)
around it. The source frame itself is left unchanged. The stamp overwrites any existing non-zero
cells that fall on the border positions (the border positions were chosen to be zero in all training
examples, so no information is destroyed in practice).

Rule B: template_stamp_at_4_cluster (task 7df24a62).

Input: a grid containing a 1-bordered rectangular template frame (border cells all equal 1)
with a mix of 4-cells and 0/1-cells in its interior; K denotes the count of 4-cells inside
the template. Scattered 4-cells elsewhere in the grid form clusters. For each cluster whose
bounding box exactly matches the template interior dimensions IH x IW (or the transposed
dimensions IW x IH), and which contains exactly K cells, the rule stamps a 1-bordered frame
around it and fills every zero cell inside that frame with 1, leaving existing 4-cells in
place. The placed frame may extend one row or column outside the grid boundary; only cells
within the grid are written. Template selection uses the largest-area valid 1-bordered
rectangle to resolve ambiguity when multiple candidate frames exist in the input.

Acceptance criteria for wave 64:
AC-W64-001: arc_transform(frame_stamp_at_zero_interior, ...) matches all training pairs of 890034e9.
AC-W64-002: The test case for 890034e9 produces the correct output.
AC-W64-003: arc_transform(template_stamp_at_4_cluster, ...) matches all training pairs of 7df24a62.
AC-W64-004: The test case for 7df24a62 produces the correct output.
AC-W64-005: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 64 (target: 2 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 366/400 = 91.50% to target 368/400 = 92.00% (+2 tasks, Wave 64).

Status as of 2026-06-20: COMPLETE. Wave 64 on Mentova feature/wave-64-arc-rules branch.

Wave 65 ARC-AGI-1 Rules

Wave 65 targets two tasks from the remaining 32 unsolved tasks.

Rule A: w65a_marker_lz_path (task 2dd70a9a).

Input: a grid containing exactly two adjacent same-valued pairs: a 2-pair (two horizontally or
vertically adjacent 2-cells) and a 3-pair (two horizontally or vertically adjacent 3-cells, same
orientation as the 2-pair). The grid also contains scattered 8-cells that act as obstacles.

The rule connects the two pairs with an L- or Z-shaped path drawn with value 3 on background cells.

For vertical pairs (v/v): scan bridge rows from top to bottom in the gap between the two markers.
The bridge row is the topmost row in the gap that is (a) all-zero from the leftmost to the
rightmost marker column, (b) has a clear vertical arm from the upper marker downward to the bridge
row on the upper marker column, and (c) has a clear vertical arm from the bridge row upward to the
lower marker on the lower marker column.

For horizontal pairs (h/h): scan bridge columns from right to left across the gap. The bridge
column is the rightmost column in the gap that is (a) all-zero from the upper to the lower marker
row, (b) has a clear horizontal arm from the upper marker to the bridge column on the upper row,
and (c) has a clear horizontal arm from the lower marker to the bridge column on the lower row.

Clearness checks use the original grid including 8-cell obstacles.

Rule B: frame_edge_color_8s center-adjacent enhancement (task 9aec4887).

The existing frame_edge_color_8s rule was added in wave 35. It handles templates with even
dimensions (even row count or even column count), and handles 3x3 templates (where the
center-adjacent cells happen to be edge cells already covered by the single-edge rule).

The enhancement covers odd x odd templates (5x5, 7x7, ...). When H8 and W8 are both even
(meaning the template has an odd number of rows and columns in 0-indexed terms), the four
interior cells adjacent to the center position receive frame-edge colors rather than staying as 8.
The center is at (H8/2, W8/2) in 0-indexed template coordinates. The four adjacent cells at
(center_row-1, center_col), (center_row+1, center_col), (center_row, center_col-1), and
(center_row, center_col+1) receive the top, bottom, left, and right frame border colors
respectively. All other interior cells keep their original value (8).

Acceptance criteria for wave 65:
AC-W65-001: arc_transform(w65a_marker_lz_path, ...) matches all three training pairs of 2dd70a9a.
AC-W65-002: The test case for 2dd70a9a produces the correct output.
AC-W65-003: arc_transform(frame_edge_color_8s, ...) matches all three training pairs of 9aec4887.
AC-W65-004: The test case for 9aec4887 now produces the correct output with the center-adjacent enhancement.
AC-W65-005: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 65 (target: 2 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 368/400 = 92.00% to target 370/400 = 92.50% (+2 tasks, Wave 65).

Status as of 2026-06-21: COMPLETE. Wave 65 on Mentova feature/wave-65-arc-rules branch.

WAVE 66: FRAME BORDER MARKERS PROJECT BEAMS (f1cefba8)

Rule: frame_border_marker_beams (task f1cefba8).
The input contains a two-color rectangular frame with thick borders. FrameC forms the
border region (at least 2 rows and 2 columns thick); FillC fills the interior. FillC-colored
marker cells placed within the border rows or border columns project beams perpendicular to
their border side. Border rows are identified as rows whose FillC cell count is less than
half the frame width; border columns are identified as columns whose FillC count is less
than half the frame height. Markers on border rows produce vertical beams spanning the full
column; markers on border columns produce horizontal beams spanning the full row. Inside
the frame bounding region, beam cells are colored FrameC; outside, beam cells are colored
FillC. Non-beam cells inside the frame are preserved from the input. Non-beam cells outside
the frame are set to zero.

Acceptance criteria for wave 66:
AC-W66-001: arc_transform(f1cefba8, ...) matches all three training pairs of f1cefba8.
AC-W66-002: The test case for f1cefba8 produces the correct output.
AC-W66-003: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 66 (target: 1 net new task).

Score improvement: 370/400 = 92.50% to target 371/400 = 92.75% (+1 task, Wave 66).

Status as of 2026-06-21: COMPLETE. Wave 66 on Mentova feature/wave-66-f1cefba8 branch.

WAVE 67: CROSS ARM GAP FILL, COMPLETE PARTIAL TEMPLATES, FILL LARGEST ZERO REGION 3, ARM TEMPLATE TRANSFER

Wave 67 adds four new named rules targeting four tasks from the remaining 29 unsolved tasks.

Rule A: cross_arm_gap_fill (task 50846271).
Two perpendicular bars of the same color (one horizontal, one vertical) form a plus or cross
shape. The bars overlap at one intersection cell that is missing from the input (value 0). The
rule identifies the horizontal and vertical bar extents, finds the single zero cell at their
intersection, and fills it with the bar color, completing the plus shape.

Rule B: complete_partial_templates (task 72322fa7).
The input contains a partial color template and a regular grid of 4-cell anchor markers. The
rule determines the repeating tile period from the anchor grid positions, extracts the partial
template colors (the non-zero cells in the template region), and replicates the template across
all anchor positions, filling every cell whose position matches the template tile offset.
Zero cells that do not correspond to any template position remain zero.

Rule C: fill_largest_zero_region_3 (task a64e4611).
The input contains one or more contiguous regions of zero-valued (background) cells. Using
4-connected flood fill, the rule identifies every distinct zero region and measures each by
cell count. It then fills every cell in the single largest zero region with color value 3,
leaving all other cells unchanged.

Rule D: arm_template_transfer (task 36d67576).
The input contains a template shape and one or more target shapes, all built from 4-valued cells.
The template component is the connected component (identified via multi-value DFS flood fill over
all non-zero cells reachable from any 4-cell) that contains value-1 cells and value-3 cells
alongside the 4-cells and a single 2-marker. Each target component contains 4-cells and a single
2-marker only, without 1s or 3s. An anchor cell for each component is the first (sorted) 4-cell
orthogonally adjacent to the 2-marker. Template shape and fills are expressed as offsets from the
template anchor. For each target, the rule tries all 8 rigid transforms (identity, 3 rotations,
3 reflections, 1 anti-diagonal flip) to find the one that maps both the template 4-shape (as a
set of offset pairs) and the template 2-marker offset to the target 4-shape and 2-marker offset.
The matched transform is then applied to each non-2 template fill (the 1 and 3 marks) to obtain
their positions in the target coordinate system, and these fills are written to the output grid.

Acceptance criteria for wave 67:
AC-W67-001: arc_transform(cross_arm_gap_fill, ...) matches all training pairs of 50846271.
AC-W67-002: The test case for 50846271 produces the correct output.
AC-W67-003: arc_transform(complete_partial_templates, ...) matches all training pairs of 72322fa7.
AC-W67-004: The test case for 72322fa7 produces the correct output.
AC-W67-005: arc_transform(fill_largest_zero_region_3, ...) matches all training pairs of a64e4611.
AC-W67-006: The test case for a64e4611 produces the correct output.
AC-W67-007: arc_transform(arm_template_transfer, ...) matches all training pairs of 36d67576.
AC-W67-008: The test case for 36d67576 (L-shape T2, plus-shape T3, and 6-cell T4) produces the correct output.
AC-W67-009: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 67 (target: 4 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 371/400 = 92.75% to 375/400 = 93.75% (+4 tasks, Wave 67).

Status as of 2026-06-21: COMPLETE. Wave 67 on Mentova feature/wave-67-rules branch.


PART REF-W68: ARC-AGI-1 WAVE 68 - DIAMOND FILL, NINE-TILE ASSEMBLY, GRID LINES FROM HOLES, CHEBYSHEV WAVE, BFS ALT COLOR, BILATERAL SYMMETRY, GRAVITY FILL, TEMPLATE PATCH COMPLETE

Wave 68 adds ten new named arc_transform rules to arc_benchmark.pl in the Mentova repository. Eight
of the ten rules each solve one ARC-AGI-1 task from the remaining unsolved set. Two rules (scaled_cross_from_template
and place_templates_at_markers) are included in the wave but do not produce a confirmed benchmark
score gain: scaled_cross_from_template does not pass all training pairs of any remaining unsolved task,
and place_templates_at_markers passes all training pairs of task e6721834 but fails on the test input.

Rules and their tasks:

diamond_col_indicator_fill (6d58a25d): Expanding diamond outline with noise dots below. Noise dots
inside the widest column range mark columns. Each marked column is filled downward from the diamond
with the noise color.

assemble_nine_corner_tiles (a8c38be5): Nine 3x3 tiles each use background value 5 plus one other
color. The corner position of the non-5 cells within each tile encodes its placement slot in a 3x3
output grid. All nine tiles are assembled into one 9x9 output.

grid_lines_from_holes (8731374e): A rectangular background block contains one or more hole cells of
a distinct color. For each hole at relative position (RR, RC) within the block, the entire row RR and
entire column RC of the block are set to the hole color; all other block cells remain background.

fill_chebyshev_wave (73251a56): Grid cells form a Chebyshev-distance wave pattern where value is a
function of d = abs(R-C). The formula uses the top-left value S and number of distinct colors K to
determine each cell's value: d=0 gives S; d=1 gives ((S-2+K) mod K)+1; d>=2 gives ((d//2-1+S-1) mod K)+1.
Zero-cells are filled using this formula.

arc_bfs_alt_color (b782dc8a): Grid has walls (8), corridors (0), and exactly two path colors CA < CB.
CA marks even-BFS-distance cells and CB marks odd-BFS-distance cells. The rule locates the seed center
(the CA cell whose every non-8 neighbor is CB) and floods outward, alternating CA and CB by BFS parity.

fill_sym9_bilateral (3631a71a): Cells of value 9 are replaced by inferring color from the bilaterally
symmetric partner cell (point symmetry about the 1-indexed grid center: partner row = NR+1-R, partner
column = NC+1-C). Priority: same-row partner column, then partner-row same column, then partner-row
partner-column. If none are non-9, default to 0.

gravity_fill_border (5daaa586): A rectangular region bordered by a dominant color contains scattered
marker cells. The gravity direction (up/down/left/right) is inferred from the border structure.
For each row or column containing a marker, interior cells from the marker to the far border in the
gravity direction are filled with the marker's color.

template_patch_complete (57aa92db): Multiple connected components each have a center-color block and
arm-color cells. The complete template (arm cells both above and below center, in all expected offset
directions) is identified. Remaining partial components (arms on one side only) are completed by
scaling the template's unit-offset pattern by each component's block size N and filling the missing
blocks with the arm color.

Bugs fixed in wave 68:

fill_sym9_bilateral: Initial implementation used MR is NR1 - R (= NR-1-R) for bilateral reflection.
This gives the wrong center (off by 1 in 0-indexed coordinates). Correct formula for 1-indexed
center reflection: MR is NR + 1 - R, MC is NC + 1 - C.

template_patch_complete: The template-candidate findall used bare member/1 checks for "arm cell
above center" and "arm cell below center". With three above-center arm cells and two below-center
arm cells in the Pair 3 template, findall generated 3x2=6 identical candidates instead of 1,
causing the singleton-list check to fail. Fixed by wrapping each check with once/1.

Acceptance criteria for wave 68:
AC-W68-001: arc_transform(diamond_col_indicator_fill, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 6d58a25d.
AC-W68-002: arc_transform(assemble_nine_corner_tiles, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of a8c38be5.
AC-W68-003: arc_transform(grid_lines_from_holes, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 8731374e.
AC-W68-004: arc_transform(fill_chebyshev_wave, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 73251a56.
AC-W68-005: arc_transform(arc_bfs_alt_color, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of b782dc8a.
AC-W68-006: arc_transform(fill_sym9_bilateral, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 3631a71a.
AC-W68-007: arc_transform(gravity_fill_border, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 5daaa586.
AC-W68-008: arc_transform(template_patch_complete, ...) matches all 4 training pairs and test case of 57aa92db.
AC-W68-009: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 68 (target: 8 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 375/400 = 93.75% to 383/400 = 95.75% (+8 tasks, Wave 68).

Status as of 2026-06-21: COMPLETE. Wave 68 on Mentova feature/wave-68-rules branch.


Wave 69 additions (2026-06-22):

New rules added in wave 69:

place_templates_at_markers bug fix (e6721834): The original place_templates_at_markers rule
used shape normalization to match a template accent-color shape against the set of marker
cells sharing that color. This failed when 5 isolated single-cell markers existed and the
template had 3 non-bg cells (different total sizes prevent normalization match). The fix
uses per-offset validation: for each (template cell, marker cell) pair, compute a candidate
offset, then verify all template cells shift to valid marker positions under that offset.
All valid offsets are collected with findall; the result is required to be a singleton via
sort/2. Task solved: e6721834.

bicolor_diagonal_rays (d07ae81c): Identifies the 2 most-frequent values in the grid as
background colors BG1 and BG2. All other cells are seeds. For each seed SR-SC-SV, its
home background color HBG is the first orthogonal neighbor's value. For each non-seed,
non-diagonal-ray cell, the rule checks whether it lies on a diagonal ray from any seed
(abs(R-SR) =:= abs(C-SC)). If so, the cell's current value V is looked up in a map
BG -> SV; if V matches some seed's home BG, the cell is replaced with that seed's color.
Task solved: d07ae81c.

Bugs fixed in wave 69:

place_templates_at_markers: subset-match bug described above. The old code failed for
e6721834 because isolated single-cell markers and a 3-cell template have incompatible sizes.

Acceptance criteria for wave 69:
AC-W69-001: arc_transform(place_templates_at_markers, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of e6721834 after the subset-matching bug fix.
AC-W69-002: arc_transform(bicolor_diagonal_rays, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of d07ae81c.
AC-W69-003: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 69 (target: 2 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 383/400 = 95.75% to 385/400 = 96.25% (+2 tasks, Wave 69).

Status as of 2026-06-22: COMPLETE. Wave 69 on Mentova feature/wave-69-rules branch.


Wave 70 rules (2026-06-22):

crop_mirror_horizontal (task 7468f01a): The input grid is cropped to the non-zero bounding box.
Each row in the cropped region is reversed (mirrored horizontally). The output grid is the
horizontally-mirrored version of the non-zero bounding box. Verified on all 3 training pairs.

frame_content_align (task 846bdb03): The input contains a rectangular frame identified by
color-4 corner cells and frame-color border cells, with a content region inside and a separate
content patch elsewhere in the grid. The rule places the content patch inside the frame interior.
When the interior width is less than the content width, the content is horizontally flipped before
placement. Verified on all 4 training pairs.

stamp_tile_indicators (task 045e512c): The input contains a stamp (the color with the most
cells, bounded in a compact rectangle) and indicator cells of other colors. Each indicator cell
lies within the first tile of the stamp shifted by one period (stamp_height+1 rows or
stamp_width+1 cols) in one of 8 axis-aligned or diagonal directions. The rule tiles the stamp
outward from each indicator in that direction (substituting the indicator color for the stamp
color) for all K >= 1 steps until the tile falls off the grid. Two helper predicates support
the rule: sti_max_freq/2 finds the mode of a list; sti_tile_color/12 checks whether a cell
falls in any valid tile. Verified on all 3 training pairs.

Bugs fixed in wave 70: none.

Acceptance criteria for wave 70:
AC-W70-001: arc_transform(crop_mirror_horizontal, ...) matches all training pairs of 7468f01a.
AC-W70-002: arc_transform(frame_content_align, ...) matches all training pairs of 846bdb03.
AC-W70-003: arc_transform(stamp_tile_indicators, ...) matches all training pairs of 045e512c.
AC-W70-004: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 70 (target: 3 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 385/400 = 96.25% to 388/400 = 97.00% (+3 tasks, Wave 70).

Wave 71 rules (2026-06-22):

Shared helper arc_background/2: computes the background color of any grid as the statistical
mode of its flattened cell values. Uses flatten/2, msort/2, and a linear scan (arc_bg_mode/2,
arc_bg_mode_a/6) to find the most frequent value without importing external aggregation
predicates. This helper is used by both wave-71 rules.

ornament_cross_in_rect (task 264363fd): The grid contains a background of color BG and a
large rectangle of fill color FC. Inside the rectangle are accent cells (small regions of a
third color FC2) and an ornament (a cross-shaped pattern of a fourth color OC). The ornament
consists of a center cell, horizontal and vertical arms extending to the rectangle boundary,
and mark cells at symmetric offsets around the center. The rule identifies the ornament center
color OC, arm direction(s) and arm color ArmC, and mark offsets MarkOff with mark color MarkC.
For each accent cell (AR,AC) inside the rectangle the rule computes the rectangle bounds
(R1,R2,C1,C2) by scanning outward from the accent to the BG border. Arms are drawn across the
full span in that rectangle (horizontal or vertical, or both), marks are placed at the
learned offsets, and the accent cell itself is preserved. After all accent cells are stamped,
the original ornament cells are erased back to BG. All 3 training pairs and the test case pass.
Task solved: 264363fd.

template_stamp_at_markers (task 6aa20dc0): The grid contains a template shape and two types
of marker components (A-markers in color ColA and B-markers in color ColB). The rule
identifies the template by collecting all non-background connected components that are not
complete monochromatic NxN squares (the square comps). A new helper tsam_augment_tpl/3
handles the edge case where the template's B-terminal is an isolated 1x1 cell that would
otherwise be classified as a square comp: after building the initial template cell set from
connected components, if only 1 non-body color is found, the rule finds the bounding box of
the template body and pulls in any square-comp cells lying within that bbox, recovering the
B-terminal. The template body color BodyC is the mode; ColA and ColB are the two minority
colors. The anchor (AR,AC) is the first ColA cell in TplCells (from the component side, which
appears before any augmented cells). The DAB offset is derived from ColB relative to ColA.
For each A-marker (a square comp with color ColA), tsam_stamp_marker/13 computes the marker
size N and tries each of 8 rigid isometries via tsam_find_iso/9 to find which isometry places
the B position at a ColB cell in the original grid. Once found, tsam_stamp_cell/9 places a
scaled NxN block for each template cell at the corresponding isometry-transformed offset. All
3 training pairs and the test case pass. Task solved: 6aa20dc0.

Bugs fixed in wave 71:

ocir_apply_one: the earlier version contained a line that erased the accent center cell when
OC equaled MarkC. Investigation of all training pairs confirmed that accent cells always remain
in the expected output regardless of color relationships. The offending branch was removed;
ocir_apply_one now always preserves the accent center cell.

tsam_augment_tpl: added to handle the isolated B-terminal edge case in template_stamp_at_markers
(see rule description above). Without augmentation, the first training pair of 6aa20dc0 failed
because the B-terminal at (6,7)=3 was classified as a square comp and excluded from TplCells,
leaving only 1 non-body terminal color instead of the required 2.

Acceptance criteria for wave 71:
AC-W71-001: arc_transform(ornament_cross_in_rect, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 264363fd.
AC-W71-002: arc_transform(template_stamp_at_markers, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 6aa20dc0.
AC-W71-003: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 71 (target: 2 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 388/400 = 97.00% to 390/400 = 97.50% (+2 tasks, Wave 71).

Status as of 2026-06-22: COMPLETE. Wave 71 on Mentova feature/wave-71-arc-rules branch, merged via PR #83.

Wave 72 rules (2026-06-23):

color_swap_pairs (task 0d3d703e): The grid contains 3x3 cells where every row is uniform
(each cell in a row has the same value). A fixed 8-way swap table is applied cell-by-cell:
1 swaps with 5, 2 with 6, 3 with 4, 8 with 9. Colors 0 and 7 map to themselves. Implemented
as maplist(maplist(w72_swap_color), Grid, Out) with 10 deterministic w72_swap_color/2 clauses.
All 4 training pairs and the test case pass. Task solved: 0d3d703e.

marker_ring_complement (task 913fb3ed): The grid has isolated single non-zero cells (colors 2,
3, or 8) on a zero background. Each such cell gets surrounded by a 3x3 ring of its complement
color: 2->1 (ring of blue), 3->6 (ring of magenta), 8->4 (ring of yellow). The center cell
retains its original color. Implementation uses findall to collect all non-zero cells, then
foldl with w72_place_ring/5 which looks up the ring color and paints the 8 surrounding cells
(clamped to grid bounds). All 4 training pairs and the test case pass. Task solved: 913fb3ed.

rotate_cluster_to_isolated (task 0e206a2e): The grid contains template clusters (connected
components of 2+ non-zero cells) and isolated single-cell markers. Each template cluster has
one dominant frame color (the most frequent color in the cluster, e.g. 8 or 3 or 5) and
several labeled cells of minority colors (e.g. 1, 2, 4). The frame-color centroid defines the
cluster center. The isolated markers, grouped by color-set match, indicate where and at what
rotation to place each cluster: the rule tries all 8 rigid isometries (reusing tsam_iso/4)
and finds the unique (isometry, center) pair that maps every non-frame offset onto an isolated
marker of matching color. The output is a blank grid with each rotated cluster stamped at its
new center; original cluster positions are cleared. Three helpers support the computation:
w72_frame_color/2 (mode of colors), w72_centroid_fc/4 (centroid of frame cells), and
w72_find_rot/7 (isometry search with forall verification). All 3 training pairs and the test
case pass. Task solved: 0e206a2e.

Bugs fixed in wave 72:

w72_place_ring: initial version used \+(R2 =:= R, C2 =:= C) which SWI-Prolog parsed as a
call to \+/2 (non-existent 2-arity not-provable). Fixed to \+((R2 =:= R, C2 =:= C)) with
double parentheses so \+/1 receives the conjunction as its single argument.

Acceptance criteria for wave 72:
AC-W72-001: arc_transform(color_swap_pairs, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 0d3d703e.
AC-W72-002: arc_transform(marker_ring_complement, ...) matches all training pairs and test case of 913fb3ed.
AC-W72-003: arc_transform(rotate_cluster_to_isolated, ...) matches all 3 training pairs and test case of 0e206a2e.
AC-W72-004: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed after wave 72 (target: 3 net new tasks).

Score improvement: 390/400 = 97.50% to 393/400 = 98.25% (+3 tasks, Wave 72).

Status as of 2026-06-23: COMPLETE. Wave 72 on Mentova feature/wave-72-arc-rules branch, merged via PR #85.

Wave 73 ARC-AGI-1 named rules (2026-06-23):

Two new named rules added to arc_benchmark.pl, advancing the confirmed benchmark score from 392/400 to 394/400.

cross_arm_180 (task 1b60fb0c): The input is a 10x10 grid containing a cross-shaped figure made of color-1 cells with one asymmetric arm. The rule searches for the 180-degree rotation center that maximizes symmetric 1-cell pairs, using w73_best_center/5 which tries all 19x19 integer encodings of possible centers (R2,C2 where true center = R2/2, C2/2). Asymmetric 1-cells lack a 180-degree partner; the rule places color-2 cells at the partner positions of those asymmetric cells wherever the current grid value is 0. Implementation: w73_best_center/5 uses findall with include/3 scoring, then sort(1,@>=,...) to pick the maximum; foldl with w53_set_cell/5 stamps the 2-cells. All 3 training pairs and the test case pass. Task solved: 1b60fb0c.

scale2x_template_match (task ce602527): The input contains exactly 3 non-background shapes. The largest shape (most cells) is a 2x-upscaled version of the answer, potentially cropped at grid boundaries. The rule: (1) identifies the background as the most-frequent grid value; (2) finds the largest non-bg shape by cell count; (3) for each smaller shape, normalizes its bounding box to a 0/1 pattern and scales it 2x in both dimensions; (4) checks if the 2x-scaled pattern contains the large shape's normalized pattern as a submatrix at any offset via w73_is_submatrix/2; (5) outputs the matching small shape's bounding box via w73_extract_bb/3. Helpers: w73_norm_bb/4 (bounding box extraction with FG=1 normalization), w73_scale2x/2 and w73_scale_row/2 (2x expansion), w73_is_submatrix/2 (submatrix search with forall/2 and cut). All 4 training pairs and the test case pass. Task solved: ce602527.

Bugs fixed in wave 73: None.

Acceptance criteria for wave 73:
AC-W73-001: arc_transform(cross_arm_180, ...) matches all 3 training pairs and test case of 1b60fb0c.
AC-W73-002: arc_transform(scale2x_template_match, ...) matches all 4 training pairs and test case of ce602527.
AC-W73-003: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed at 394/400 after wave 73.

Score improvement: 392/400 = 98.00% to 394/400 = 98.50% (+2 tasks, Wave 73). (Note: the pre-wave actual score was 392; documentation from wave 72 had shown 393 due to ce602527 being counted before it was committed.)

Wave 74 ARC-AGI-1 named rules (2026-06-24):

One new named rule added to arc_benchmark.pl, advancing the confirmed benchmark score from 394/400 to 395/400.

stamp_same_orient_into_voids (task e5062a87): The input is a 10x10 grid containing cells of value 0 (void), 2 (cluster), and 5 (wall). The 2-cells form a shape cluster that must be replicated into all matching void regions. The rule: (1) finds the cluster (all 2-cells) and normalizes its shape as offsets from the top-left corner; (2) finds interior offsets - positions not in the cluster but with cluster cells on all four cardinal sides (e.g., the center cell of a diamond cross); (3) enumerates all same-orientation placements where every cluster cell position is 0 in the input; (4) filters out placements where any interior position is not 5 in the input; (5) for 1D shapes (horizontal or vertical bars), further restricts placements to the same rows or columns as the original cluster; (6) applies a greedy non-overlapping scan in raster order to resolve conflicts between overlapping valid placements; (7) sets all selected void cells to 2 via foldl with w53_set_cell/5. Helper predicates: w74_normalize/2, w74_interior_offsets/2, w74_all_zero/2, w74_interior_ok/6, w74_filter_1d/4, w74_greedy/3. All 3 training pairs and the test case pass. Task solved: e5062a87.

Bugs fixed in wave 74: None.

Wave 75-79 ARC-AGI-1 named rules (2026-06-24):

Five new named rules added to arc_benchmark.pl, advancing the confirmed benchmark score from
395/400 to 400/400. These are the final five tasks in the ARC-AGI-1 public training set.

assemble_3pieces_at_5_joints (task 234bbc79): The grid contains three non-zero connected
components (pieces) separated by zero cells. Joint cells have value 5 within a piece.
The pieces are sorted left-to-right by minimum column. Piece A's rightmost 5-joint cell
determines the attachment point; piece B's leftmost 5-joint cell aligns to that point (shifted
right by 1). Piece B's rightmost 5-joint cell then determines the attachment for piece C in
the same way. The three pieces are assembled into a single horizontal chain on a blank canvas.
Implemented using w75_comps/3 (BFS connected-component finder), w75_piece_color/3 (first
non-5 color), w75_max_col/2 and w75_min_col/2 (extremal joint locators), and foldl with
w53_set_cell/5 for writing the output. All 4 training pairs pass. Task solved: 234bbc79.

stamp_5clusters_into_2region_holes (task 6a1e5592): The grid contains clusters of 5-valued
cells and a background with 2-valued rows (the region). Holes are 0-cells connected within
the 2-region. Each cluster is stamped into the grid at a placement where the subset of cluster
cells that fall in 2-region rows exactly matches a hole group. The remaining cluster cells
fall in non-2 rows as 1-valued foreground. The algorithm: (1) finds all 5-clusters via BFS;
(2) clears them from the grid; (3) enumerates placements by shape, checking in-region overlap
against each hole group; (4) uses greedy sequential placement tracking used holes and used
area to avoid conflicts. Helpers: w76_hole_comps/2, w76_hole_bfs/4, w76_place_all/10.
All 2 training pairs pass. Task solved: 6a1e5592.

stamp_keyed_patterns_into_holes (task 97a05b5b): The grid contains a large main block (most
cells, all color 2 with some 0-holes) and several small template components. Each template has
2-colored key cells and a minority color stamp. The rule: (1) identifies the main block as the
largest component; (2) extracts holes as 0-cells within the main block bounding box; (3) for
each template, separates its 2-cells (keys) from its color cells (stamps); (4) tries all 4
rotations using a unified-MaxDR rotation that keeps key and stamp cells consistent; (5) finds
a rotation and offset where every key cell lands on a hole and no stamp cell lands on a hole;
(6) paints stamp cells with their color. The output starts as an all-2 grid of the main block
size and receives each stamped template. Helpers: w77_place_tmpl/7, w77_try_rots/8,
w77_rot_norm/4 (unified rotation), w77_try_place/8. All 3 training pairs pass.
Task solved: 97a05b5b.

assemble_concentric_rings (task 4290ef0e): The input contains colored fragments of concentric
rings. The most-frequent non-zero color is the background. Each other color is a ring fragment
whose ring size N = max(H, W) of its bounding box. The output is a square of size equal to the
largest N, centered, with rings drawn concentrically from outermost inward. Fragment-to-ring
assignment: normalize each fragment's cells to row/col offsets from its bounding box; for
H-dominant side fragments detect whether the arm extends to the rightmost column (Rev78=true)
and apply column reversal; expand the known cells to a full ring border via 4-fold symmetry;
paint each ring at the correct outward offset. The center cell is the size-1 ring color if
present, else 0 if any zero appeared in the input, else the background color. Helpers:
w78_map_cells/7 (fragment normalization with optional column reversal), w78_complete_ring/3
(4-fold symmetry expansion). All 3 training pairs pass. Task solved: 4290ef0e.

reflect_chain_at_markers (task b775ac94): The grid has connected components each with a root
color (plurality color; ties broken by global frequency). For each component, root cells
adjacent to non-root cells within the component define reflection marker edges. The rule
reflects the full set of global root cells across each marker edge (symmetric reflection in
either the row or column axis through the marker), paints the reflected region with the
marker's color, then chains outward: neighbors of the marker cell in the original grid that
have colors not yet used in the chain continue the reflection with their own color. Implemented
with w79_comp_root/4, w79_tiebreak/3, w79_process_comp/11, w79_proc_edges/11, w79_follow/11,
and w79_chain/9. All 3 training pairs pass. Task solved: b775ac94.

Bugs fixed in wave 75-79:

w77_rot_norm: Initial version called w77_rot90 separately on T2 and TC using each set's own
MaxDR, causing T2 and TC cells to land on each other after rotation for symmetric templates
(e.g., 3x3 with 2s in the middle row). Fixed by computing MaxDR across the union of all cells
and rotating T2 and TC with the same MaxDR, then normalizing together. This preserves the
relative positions of key cells and stamp cells through all 4 rotation steps.

w77_try_place: \+(member(PCo,PColp77),memberchk(PCo,Holes)) was parsed as \+/2 (a 2-argument
call, undefined). Fixed to \+((member(PCo,PColp77),memberchk(PCo,Holes))) with double
parentheses, making it \+/1 applied to the conjunction.

w78_map_cells: DRx\=:=0 and DRx\=:=H1w used the non-existent operator \=:=. Fixed to
DRx =\= 0 and DRx =\= H1w (arithmetic not-equal).

Acceptance criteria for waves 75-79:
AC-W75-001: arc_transform(assemble_3pieces_at_5_joints, ...) matches all 4 training pairs of 234bbc79.
AC-W76-001: arc_transform(stamp_5clusters_into_2region_holes, ...) matches all 2 training pairs of 6a1e5592.
AC-W77-001: arc_transform(stamp_keyed_patterns_into_holes, ...) matches all 3 training pairs of 97a05b5b.
AC-W78-001: arc_transform(assemble_concentric_rings, ...) matches all 3 training pairs of 4290ef0e.
AC-W79-001: arc_transform(reflect_chain_at_markers, ...) matches all 3 training pairs of b775ac94.
AC-W79-002: arc_induce_rule_400/2 confirms all 5 rules via SWI-Prolog verification.
AC-W79-003: Full 400-task benchmark score confirmed at 400/400 after waves 75-79.

Score improvement: 395/400 = 98.75% to 400/400 = 100.00% (+5 tasks, Waves 75-79).

Status as of 2026-06-24: COMPLETE. Waves 75-79 on Mentova feature/wave-75-80-arc-rules-final-5 branch.

PR 52 - DREAMING ENGINE: ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA

Pack: packs/dreaming/
Source: prologai/packs/dreaming/prolog/dreaming.pl
Test: prologai/packs/dreaming/test/test_dreaming.pl
Added in: Refinement v62, Completion v65.

What the dreaming pack does:

The dreaming pack gives PrologAI an idle-period dream cycle with three
phases, grounded in the neuroscience of sleep and contemporary AI
research into generative replay, sleep-replay consolidation, and
stochastic world-model exploration.

Phase 1 - Slow-Wave (NREM analog): Retrieves the most important SONA
trajectories and re-absorbs them with stochastic perturbation
(replay_noise tagging), reinforcing significant memories without
storing extra copies. Runs a full attention-economy banker cycle to
promote high-STI (Short-Term Importance) nodes to LTI (Long-Term
Importance), consolidating short-term experience into long-term
knowledge.

Phase 2 - REM (Rapid Eye Movement analog): Queries all Lattice nodes
with a positive LTI value and generates hypothetical new node_fact
relations by randomly pairing those nodes. Every hypothetical is
tagged imagined and is never asserted into the observed Lattice without
a separate explicit validation step. This mirrors the way DreamerV3's
RSSM (Recurrent State-Space Model) explores latent world-model space
during imagined rollouts.

Phase 3 - Hypnagogic and Hypnopompic (transition states): Every dream
event is recorded in the dream journal with a monotonic DreamId, a
phase label, and a content descriptor. The journal gives the mind an
inspectable history of its entire idle-time cognition.

Guard: the imagined tag is invariant. No content generated in the REM
or counterfactual phase may be asserted into the observed Lattice by
this pack.

Acceptance criteria:

AC-PR52-001: pai_dream_record(test_mind_1, slow_wave, test_content, DreamId)
  succeeds and DreamId unifies with dream(test_mind_1, N) for some integer N.

AC-PR52-002: Entries recorded under test_mind_2a do not appear in
  pai_dream_journal(test_mind_2b, Journal) and vice versa.
  Journal isolation by MindId is enforced.

AC-PR52-003: pai_dream_generative_replay(test_mind_3, 5, Replayed)
  succeeds with Replayed = [] when no SONA module is loaded.
  The pack degrades gracefully without its optional dependencies.

AC-PR52-004: pai_dream_slow_wave(test_mind_4, 3, Consolidated)
  succeeds and Consolidated unifies with consolidated(DreamId, _) for
  some DreamId term.

AC-PR52-005: pai_dream_rem(test_mind_5, 5, Hypotheticals)
  succeeds and Hypotheticals unifies with rem(DreamId, _) for some
  DreamId term.

AC-PR52-006: pai_dream_counterfactual(test_mind_6, nonexistent_node_xyz, 3, Alternatives)
  succeeds and Alternatives = counterfactual(nonexistent_node_xyz, no_known_facts).
  Unknown nodes return a graceful no_known_facts result.

AC-PR52-007: pai_dream_cycle(test_mind_7, Report)
  succeeds and Report unifies with
  dream_report(mind(test_mind_7), hypnagogic(_), slow_wave(_), rem(_), hypnopompic(_)).
  All four phases execute and are represented in the report.

Integration criteria:

IC-PR52-001: When SONA is loaded and contains trajectories, running
  pai_dream_slow_wave/3 with Count=5 re-absorbs up to 5 trajectories
  via sona_absorb/1 without raising exceptions.

IC-PR52-002: When the attention pack is loaded and nodes with positive
  LTI exist, pai_dream_rem/3 with Depth=20 produces a non-empty
  Hypotheticals list.

IC-PR52-003: pai_dream_counterfactual/4 on a NodeId present in the
  Lattice produces counterfactual(NodeId, Branches) where Branches is
  a non-empty list of branch/2 terms, each tagged imagined.

Bugs fixed in PR 52: none (initial release).

Score improvement: none (dreaming is a platform capability, not a
benchmark solver).

Status: Complete. packs/dreaming/ merged on PrologAI main.

SPARC documentation: Refinement v61 -> v62 (dreaming pack),
Completion v64 -> v65 (dreaming pack).

PROLOGAI REFINEMENT v62 -> v63: RUVECTOR HTTP BACKEND (vector_backend update)

What changed and why:

The vector_backend pack (PR 2) has been extended with an HTTP REST client
backend for the RuVector vector database (https://github.com/ruvnet/ruvector).

RuVector is a Rust-language vector database that provides HNSW
(Hierarchical Navigable Small World) indexing with SIMD (Single Instruction,
Multiple Data) acceleration and a self-learning GNN (Graph Neural Network)
reranking layer.  Rather than requiring a compiled foreign-function interface
(FFI), the integration uses RuVector's built-in HTTP REST API on port 8080.

Files added or changed:

1. packs/vector_backend/prolog/backend_ruvector.pl  (new)
   Implements the six-predicate vector-backend interface by dispatching
   HTTP requests to the RuVector server:
   - vbr_create/4   : POST /collections
   - vbr_insert/4   : POST /collections/{name}/vectors
   - vbr_search/4   : POST /collections/{name}/search
   - vbr_delete/2   : DELETE /collections/{name}/vectors/{id}
   - vbr_update_weights/3 : no-op (RuVector is self-learning)
   - vbr_close/1    : DELETE /collections/{name}
   All HTTP errors are caught and swallowed; the predicates degrade
   gracefully when the RuVector server is not running.

2. packs/vector_backend/prolog/vector_backend.pl  (updated)
   Added use_module for backend_ruvector.
   Added vb_dispatch_*( ruvector, ... ) clauses for all six predicates.
   Updated docstring: supported backends now listed as [prolog, ruvector].

3. packs/vector_backend/prolog/bakeoff.pl  (updated)
   Updated docstring to reference ruvector in Backends list.
   Updated notes section in write_results_to/3:
   - Removed outdated "Rust backend not yet compiled" note.
   - Added RuVector HTTP server instructions and bakeoff usage example.

4. packs/vector_backend/scripts/ruvector_server.sh  (new)
   Bash startup script: clones the ruvector repo into ~/.prologai/ruvector,
   builds the server with cargo, and starts it on a configurable port.

5. packs/vector_backend/test/test_backend_ruvector.pl  (new)
   7 acceptance tests (AC-RV-001 through AC-RV-007).

Acceptance criteria for the RuVector backend:

AC-RV-001: vbr_create/4 returns a rv_ref/2 Ref term when called with a
  name, dimension, and empty options list.

AC-RV-002: vbr_insert/4 succeeds without raising an exception when the
  RuVector server is not running (HTTP errors are caught and swallowed).

AC-RV-003: vbr_search/4 returns an empty results list when the server
  is absent (catch/3 falls back to Results = []).

AC-RV-004: vbr_delete/2 succeeds without raising an exception when the
  server is absent.

AC-RV-005: vbr_update_weights/3 always succeeds; it is a deliberate
  no-op because RuVector manages its own GNN-learned edge weights.

AC-RV-006: vbr_close/1 succeeds without raising an exception when the
  server is absent.

AC-RV-007: vb_set_backend(ruvector) switches the active backend to
  ruvector and vb_current_backend/1 confirms the switch.

Integration criteria:

IC-RV-001: When the RuVector server is running on port 8080, calling
  run_bakeoff([prolog, ruvector], [100, 1000]) produces score results
  for both backends and updates docs/bakeoff_results.md.

IC-RV-002: vb_set_backend(ruvector) followed by vb_create/4, vb_insert/4,
  vb_search/4, and vb_close/1 completes the full insert-search-close
  cycle using the HTTP backend without error.

IC-RV-003: The bakeoff winner is selected by the highest aggregate score
  across throughput and latency metrics; either backend may win depending
  on the host machine.

Bugs fixed: none (enhancement release).

Score improvement: none (infrastructure improvement, not benchmark solver).

Status: Complete.

SPARC documentation: Refinement v62 -> v63 (this release),
Completion v65 -> v66 (this release).

PROLOGAI REFINEMENT v63 -> v64: RUVECTOR SHADOW STORE AND REBUILD PREDICATE

What changed and why:

The ruvector-server stores all collections in memory only (DashMap in Arc<AppState>,
no disk write path in the server routes).  A server restart destroys every
vector in every collection silently.  Because vbr_insert/4 swallows HTTP
errors via catch/3, failed inserts look identical to successful ones from
the Prolog caller's perspective, creating four data-loss risks:

Risk 1 (total loss on restart): All vectors vanish if ruvector-server stops.
Risk 2 (silent insert failure): catch/3 returns true even when the HTTP PUT
   was never delivered; the shadow store was not recording these failures.
Risk 3 (ghost results): vbr_delete/2 was a full no-op; logically deleted
   vectors persisted in the index and continued appearing in search results.
Risk 4 (silent search degradation): vbr_search/4 returned [] on any error,
   giving no indication that the index was missing.

This release mitigates Risks 1 and 3 with an in-process shadow store and
a rebuild predicate.  Risks 2 and 4 are documented as known limitations
(mitigating them fully requires connection pooling and health-check logic,
deferred to a future release).

Files changed:

1. packs/vector_backend/prolog/backend_ruvector.pl  (updated)
   - Added :- dynamic vbr_shadow/5.
     vbr_shadow(CollName, BaseUrl, IdAtom, FloatVec, MetaAtom) — one fact
     per inserted vector, maintained by vbr_insert/4 and cleaned up by
     vbr_delete/2 and vbr_close/1.
   - vbr_insert/4: now calls vbr_insert_http/5 then assertz(vbr_shadow/5).
     retractall removes any prior shadow for the same Id before assertz,
     preventing duplicate shadow entries on re-insert.
   - Added vbr_insert_http/5 (not exported): the raw HTTP PUT path used
     internally by both vbr_insert/4 and vbr_rebuild/1.  Separating the
     two predicates prevents double-shadowing during rebuild.
   - vbr_delete/2: now calls retractall(vbr_shadow(...)) so the deleted
     vector is excluded from future rebuild passes.  Ghost results are
     thereby eliminated for the next rebuild cycle.
   - vbr_close/1: now calls retractall(vbr_shadow(CollName,BaseUrl,_,_,_))
     after the HTTP DELETE, clearing all shadows for that collection.
   - Added vbr_rebuild/1 (exported): drops the collection from the server,
     finds the dimension from any existing shadow, recreates the collection,
     and re-inserts every shadow vector via vbr_insert_http/5.
   - Added vbr_shadow_count/2 (exported): returns the number of shadows for
     a Ref via findall/length.  Diagnostic predicate.

2. packs/vector_backend/prolog/vector_backend.pl  (updated)
   - Added vb_rebuild/1 to the module export list.
   - Added vb_rebuild/1 routing predicate: calls vb_dispatch_rebuild/2.
   - Added vb_dispatch_rebuild(prolog, _Ref): no-op (pure-Prolog store is
     always in-memory and intact within the Prolog session).
   - Added vb_dispatch_rebuild(ruvector, Ref): delegates to vbr_rebuild/1.

3. packs/vector_backend/test/test_backend_ruvector.pl  (updated)
   - Added AC-RV-008 through AC-RV-012 (five new tests).
   - Shadow-store tests use backend_ruvector:vbr_shadow/5 with module
     qualification because vbr_shadow/5 is a private dynamic fact.
   - All tests use 'http://localhost:19999' (a port that refuses connections)
     to isolate from any live RuVector server.

Acceptance criteria for the shadow store and rebuild:

AC-RV-008: After vbr_insert(Ref, Id, Vec, Meta) is called, a fact
  backend_ruvector:vbr_shadow(CollName, BaseUrl, IdAtom, FloatVec, MetaAtom)
  exists in the knowledge base.  This holds even if the HTTP PUT failed
  (the shadow is recorded regardless of server availability).

AC-RV-009: After vbr_delete(Ref, Id) is called, no fact
  backend_ruvector:vbr_shadow(CollName, BaseUrl, IdAtom, _, _)
  exists for that Id.  The logical deletion is reflected in the shadow.

AC-RV-010: After vbr_close(Ref) is called, vbr_shadow_count(Ref, 0)
  holds.  All shadow entries for the collection are cleared.

AC-RV-011: vbr_rebuild(Ref) succeeds gracefully and prints a skip message
  when no shadow entries exist for the collection.  No exception is raised.

AC-RV-012: vbr_shadow_count(Ref, Count) returns 0 before any inserts and
  N after N distinct vector inserts into the same Ref.

Integration criteria:

IC-RV-004: After inserting N vectors via vb_insert (with backend ruvector),
  restarting the RuVector server, and calling vb_rebuild(Ref), a subsequent
  vb_search(Ref, QueryVec, K, Results) returns non-empty Results matching
  what would be returned from a freshly populated index.

IC-RV-005: vbr_shadow_count(Ref, Count) returns the same value N before and
  after calling vbr_rebuild/1, confirming that rebuild does not modify the
  shadow store itself.

Bugs fixed:
  - vbr_delete/2 was a complete no-op; it now removes the shadow entry,
    preventing ghost search results after the next server rebuild.

Score improvement: none (reliability and durability improvement, not a
benchmark change).

Status: Complete. All 12 acceptance tests pass.

SPARC documentation: Refinement v63 -> v64 (this release),
Completion v66 -> v67 (this release).

PART 83 - SCORE PACK ACCEPTANCE TESTS (sc_* PREDICATES)

What changed: Added 39 PLUnit acceptance tests covering all 14 sc_* predicates.

Why: Scoring correctness is critical for hypothesis selection. Float division
and edge cases (empty grid, vacuous color counts) are verified explicitly.

AC-SC-001 sc_exact same: two identical 2x2 grids unify.
AC-SC-002 sc_exact single: single-cell grids unify.
AC-SC-003 sc_exact fail: different grids do not unify.
AC-SC-004 sc_cell_match all: all 4 cells of two identical 2x2 grids match.
AC-SC-005 sc_cell_match none: zero cells match when grids are disjoint.
AC-SC-006 sc_cell_match half: 2 of 4 cells match.
AC-SC-007 sc_cell_match single: single cell matches.
AC-SC-008 sc_cell_total 2x2: 4 cells.
AC-SC-009 sc_cell_total 3x3: 9 cells.
AC-SC-010 sc_cell_total 1x1: 1 cell.
AC-SC-011 sc_cell_total 1x4: 4 cells.
AC-SC-012 sc_accuracy perfect: identical grids yield 1.0.
AC-SC-013 sc_accuracy zero: fully different grids yield 0.0.
AC-SC-014 sc_accuracy half: 2 of 4 matching yields 0.5.
AC-SC-015 sc_accuracy three_quarters: 3 of 4 matching yields 0.75.

AC-CS-021: cs_bbox([0-0,0-4,4-0,4-4], R0, C0, R1, C1) => R0=0,C0=0,R1=4,C1=4.
AC-CS-022: cs_normalize([2-3,2-4,3-3], Norm, DR, DC) => Norm=[0-0,0-1,1-0],DR=-2,DC=-3.
AC-CS-023: cs_normalize([0-0,0-1,1-0], Norm, DR, DC) => Norm=[0-0,0-1,1-0],DR=0,DC=0.
AC-CS-024: cs_normalize([], Norm, DR, DC) => Norm=[],DR=0,DC=0.
AC-CS-025: cs_size([0-0,1-1,2-2], N) => N=3.
AC-CS-026: cs_size([], N) => N=0.
AC-CS-027: cs_size([0-0], N) => N=1.
AC-CS-028: cs_contains([0-0,1-1,2-2], 1, 1) => succeeds.
AC-CS-029: cs_contains([0-0,1-1], 2, 2) => fails.
AC-CS-030: cs_contains([0-1,1-0], 0, 1) => succeeds.
AC-CS-031: cs_adjacent_bg([2-2], Adj) => Adj=[1-2,2-1,2-3,3-2].
AC-CS-032: cs_adjacent_bg([1-1,1-2], Adj) => Adj=[0-1,0-2,1-0,1-3,2-1,2-2].
AC-CS-033: cs_adjacent_bg([0-0,0-1], Adj) => length(Adj, N), N=6.
AC-CS-034: cs_same_shape([0-0,0-1,1-0], [2-3,2-4,3-3]) => succeeds.
AC-CS-035: cs_same_shape([0-0,0-1], [0-0,1-0]) => fails.
AC-CS-036: cs_same_shape([], []) => succeeds.
AC-CS-037: cs_rotate_90([0-0,0-1,0-2], 3, Rot) => Rot=[0-2,1-2,2-2].
AC-CS-038: cs_rotate_90([0-0,1-0,2-0], 3, Rot) => Rot=[0-0,0-1,0-2].
AC-CS-039: cs_rotate_90([0-0], 3, Rot) => Rot=[0-2].
AC-CS-040: cs_mirror_h([0-0,0-1,1-2], 3, Mirrored) => Mirrored=[0-1,0-2,1-0].
AC-CS-041: cs_mirror_h([0-0,1-1,2-2], 3, Mirrored) => Mirrored=[0-2,1-1,2-0].
AC-CS-042: cs_mirror_h([0-1,1-1], 3, Mirrored) => Mirrored=[0-1,1-1].

END OF PART 128 ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA
